<Author>Natla
<Content>Lives up to the reviews I always use trip advisor reviews as a guide on where to stay and booked this hotel based on the good feed back on this site. On the whole the is a very nice hotel in a good location. Central Park and Time Sq are both walkable. Also after a long day of shopping and sight seeing it was nice to be uptown away from the traffic and beeping but still close to bars and restaurants. The beacon has a small, personal and boutique feel to it, even though it has well over 20 floors and is quite large. I prefer this compared to hotel which are so large you feel like a statistic. The evening staff on reception where up beat, friendly and helpful, where as the mangers in the morning where not. We stayed In a newly refurbished room which had a lovely design, was clean and fresh plus the maid service was good. Not sure I would be happy paying $240 per night for the old unfurnished style room, so well worth asking in advance which type of room you will be staying in.

<Author>JoeM_8
<Content>Wouldn't atay anywhere else in Manahattan Over the past ten years, we have stayed at Hotel Beacon four times and - having stayed at some other hotels - we would never stay anywhere else in NYC,The rooms are huge and very comfortable with a small but well-equipped kitchenette.It's a great location, stunning views to Central Park or the Hudson from the upper floors - don't forget to ask when booking because they do try to give you what you request; buses and subway within moments of the door - or just walk to Columbus, Amsterdam, Central Park, even Mid -Town.One particularly brilliant aspect of Hotel Beacon: Fairways foodstore directly across Broadway from the Beacon. a jaw-dropping selection of stuff to eat, including a hot food counter which makes eating in any restaurant a bit of a waste of time: grab a bottle of wine at the Beacon Liquor store, Korean chicken or something at Fairways then dine at your Hotel Beacon room window overlooking a million Manhattan lights. Unforgetable.Frankly at these prices there is no point in staying anywhere else, particularly if you fancy experiencing the rather attractive life of an Upper Westside New Yorker!

<Author>vandynurse
<Content>My new favorite NYC hotel My husband and I very much enjoyed our 4 night stay at this hotel over the Thanksgiving Holiday. We had a one bedroom suite - very large even by non NY standards. It had a complete but small kitchen with stove/oven , microwave and fridge. Bed was comfortable- not too hard or soft but just right. We were told it was a newly renovated room. Everything looked very fresh and new. Housekeeping did a great job- room was clean and restocked with towels, tea, ect everytime we came back in the afternoon. There was a tea kettle which was a very nice touch- I used it everyday. The shower was adequate. The staff was very nice and efficient. Any time we had a problem(couldn't get TV to work ) maintenance would arrive in just a few minutes to fix the problem. Great location-subway, grocery store, and shops are very close by. Even on the 23rd floor you can still hear the traffic- but this is NYC- so bring earplugs if you are a light sleeper. When we were in the living room area we could occassionally hear the TV /conversation of the people next door. However we never heard any noise(other than traffic) in the bedroom. I don't know if all the one bedroom suites are configered like ours- but the bathroom could only be accessed by going thru the bedroom. This is a very small neg- but if you are traveling with other people they would have to go thru your bedroom to get to the bath. The Beacon had everything I needed and wanted in a hotel. It was a very good value. We will be staying there the next time we visit NYC.

<Author>pabl01neum
<Content>Nice Hotel The Beacon Hotel is just a short walk from the 72nd and Broadway subway stop (convenient). Check-in was friendly and prompt. The elevator was a bit clunky, but overall OK.The room (908) was located directly across from the elevator. The door was not particularly sound-proof, so we heard people coming and going all night. Fortunately, their were no big parties during our 3-night stay, so we slept fairly well.The room was acceptable and reasonably clean. The room had a nice flat screen TV that required some study before we could operate it properly. Internet access was $9.95 per 24 hours (reasonable speed) - I can't understand why hotels still insist on ripping off guests on internet access. Curtains blacked out the room fairly well. The bed was a double not a queen, but was fairly comfortable. We had a nice little kitchenette with microwave, sink, stovetop, coffee maker, refrigerator.The bathroom was OK. The toilet had a leak to the rear that was creating a rust spot. They were not cleaning the leaking area properly which made the spot evident. Shower had OK flow. The sink was located in the bathroom. No fan in the bathroom leading to a very steamed-up room  mirrors after a shower.Check out was fast. Concierge was knowledgeable and courteous.

<Author>anotherlife
<Content>Retreat to the Upper West Side We just got back yesterday after a four day stay here and really could not be happier. The hotel is a quiet (if New York is ever quiet) retreat from the bustle of the tourist areas.This hotel is recently updated in quiet shades of green and neutral colors. It has nice flat screen TVs and pretty dang comfy beds! It's clean with nothing scary in the bathroom! t's almost directly on the 1,2,3 subway line and you can get just abut anywhere from there. We sure did!We stayed in a one bedroom with two double beds in the actual bedroom and the living room had a pull out couch. The beds were great, not so much the couch, but that's usually true with any pull out! Yes, I said a bedroom, totally separate from the living area. It was great. They have other configurations too. You can have access to the health club for an extra $20 per person a day. We did not find this a necessary expense so I can't tell you anything about the club. The gift shop (or it used to be a gift shop) is undergoing remodeling and I'm not sure what the outcome of that will be. It was a vast empty spot when we were there. There is a theater right next door also called the Beacon but it is seriously in need of rennovation and is not open. All of the rooms have a tiny little kitchen with a smaller size refrigerator, a tiny stove with an oven, a microwave and a little sink. There is a toaster too along with dishes, a couple of cooking pans and silverware. This was very nice to have and we used it every day for breakfast rather than try and all get completely dressed and ready and then go somewhere for breakfast. There is a wonderful market (Fairway) directly across the street. It has everything you need and plenty you don't need but wil buy anyway!There is also a wine and spirits store on the corner and a decent restaurant right next door. There is a Lohman's across the street which was handy when my daughter forgot to pack her leggings. We just ran over there and picked up a pair for $6.99. Walk up the street and you are at a great bagle shop, HH. Be warned, they only take cash, but have an ATM right in the store! Central Park is also only a few blocks away. Big Nick's Pizza and Burgers is up the street a block or two. Good pizza, didn't try the burgers.The neighborhood is pleasant and we never felt unsafe walking in the area. The building is 25 stories and our room was on the 23rd floor. We paid about $380/night for this room. I thought it was a bargain considering the prices near Times Square, the size of the room and the fact that there was a kitchen. In fact, after spending time in the busier areas, I was really glad we chose to stay at the Beacon. Just coming up from the subway into the neighborhood was calming, especially at night. I liked it.The front desk at check in was nice. Didn't deal with them much after that. There is a Concierge but we didn't find them terribly useful. We weren't really depending on them for anything so that wasn't a big deal. Could be an issue if you really wanted them to do something for you. We could have caught them on a bad day too, you just never know for sure.Overall this was a great stay. I would not hesitate to stay here again or to recommend it to others.  
<Date>Oct 13, 2008

<Author>sh0psh0psh0p
<Content>Super My daughter and I have just returned from a four night stay in hotel Beacon. I booked the hotel on account for the reviews on this site and hoped for a refurbished room. We got a room on the 9th floor and this floor was finished. Alas the room was on the backside so the view was disappointing. But whatever, you are in New York and spent only a little time in your room, which was really excellent. King size beds and tastfully furnished and even a little kitchen, which we did not use, you can eat everywhere, but the refrigerator is nice for a cold drink.The neighbourhood is really nice, you stay among the residents and it is nice to see how the New Yorkers live in their really great appartments. When we arrived with the Super Shuttle (was not as bad as I read in the reviews) I was afraid the hotel was too far from everything (in 2000 I stayed in hotel Edison en Milford Plaza), but no, the metro is very nearby, and even walking was not a crime because there are shops everywhere. The staff is friendly but not over the top, (Americans are really excessive polite, we are not used to that in Holland. We think just being polite is enough) and the concierges are very helpfull.Midtown is the part of New York we liked fewest, very crowded. We liked the Lower East Side, Soho, Greenwich Village en East Village better. Less crowded and many nice little boutiques.If you have time enough take the L-train to Bedford av in Brooklyn, is is a long street with really nice boutiques and restaurants.But alas our trip is over, but when I visit New York again I will surely stay in hotel Beacon.

<Author>joniUk
<Content>Recommended My wife and I booked a week in August through Virgin Atlantic and chose the Beacon as it seemed to offer good value for money and had good reviews, and we weren't disappointed. Although our room wasn't the largest it was exceptionally clean and quiet with a superb kitchenette area that had all the equipment you could need. The lack of an onsite restaurant is not an issue as the Viand Cafe next door opens at 6:30 and shuts late. It has an extensive menu and provides breakfasts that will set you up for the day. If you were of a lazy disposition you could eat here all week and not finish the menu.Be sure to go to the Fairway supermarket opposite, it's everything a food store should be.

<Author>CrunchNottingham
<Content>Bit out of town but has good subway links and close to some good food outlets The hotel Beacon was still being refurbished when we checked in on the 25th of August. Virgin informed me that the work was running behind schedule but would be completed by 31st of August - it wasn't and they still had floors 1 through 7 to complete. My husband and I went to NY with 6 friends and out of the 4 couples only 1 was initially give a refurbished room. We did complain and they were helpful and moved the rest of us on the following day. So when you book in if you're given a room on floors 1 through 7 ask for a higher floor. The lower floors are clean but very very tired and in need of quite a lot of work. Apart from that the Beacon is in a really good location and is situated between the 72nd and 79th subway stations so getting around NY is easy and cheap. A single trip being $2 on the subway. If you're planning to use the subway get a metro ticket as the most economical way to travel. If you want a really excellent, and cheap breakfast you must go to Big Niks - the d茅cor leaves a lot to be desired but the food and staff are excellent. An excellent place for an evening meal is Niko's and if you tell then you're staying at the Beacon you even get 10% discount from the bill. The Vind Cafe is ok and right next door to the hotel - the foods good and plentiful but the service is dire and they add a huge service charge on the bill.

<Author>gefilte63
<Content>A- I had two separate stays in July at the Beacon--one for five nights, and one for three nights. Overall it was a very good experience although a little uneven. When I first entered my room on the eighth floor I was thrilled to see a two room suite with kitchenette, lots of closets and a nice bathroom. I had a nice view overlooking Broadway. At 7:20 am I was awakened by what I thought were bowling balls being dropped on the floor above me. Tried as I might to go back to sleep (it was my only chance to sleep in) the noise was too much. I finally got on an elevator and went up one floor to see a huge construction zone. Yes, the HB is undergoing renovations...that start at 7:20 in the morning. I asked to be switched to another room and was moved down to a nearly identical room on the 7th floor. For my troubles, I got a week's free wireless. Even so, the walls are thin and the room was not the quietest. It also took 24 hours and three requests to get a lightbulb in the bathroom replaced.On my second stay (two days later) I got a room on 19 in the already renovated section. Although I was in a much smaller room--not a two-room suite--the quality was vastly superior: nicer linens and mattress, flat screen TV, even the toiletries in the bathroom were upgraded. The lesson here: request a room above the construction zone!The neighborhood is great. Fairway supermarket right across the street, tons of restaurants and easy access to subways at 72 and 79, taxis and buses. It is safe as well.I would definitely stay here again. The staff was friendly and mostly attentive. The location is excellent. The price is right.

<Author>charlesct
<Content>Spacious and homey with some minor service lapses Stayed here for ten days at the end of July while attending a conference in Morningside Heights. I had a one bedroom king suite; my wife joined me for the last three days.I was pleased upon entering the room to see that it was obviously newly-renovated. It was much nicer than the pictures on either the hotel's own website or the traveler photos here. The new rooms are in a kind of Art Deco style with earth tones predominating, and have (in the suites) two large flat-screen TVs.The suites are quite spacious and it was very pleasant to stay here for such a long time. The kitchenette (sink, fridge, oven and range, microwave) meant we could eat breakfast, snacks, and some meals in the room. There was a full service for four as well as pots, pans, some cutlery and a toaster -- none of which we actually used.Wi-Fi worked well though it was annoying to pay $9.95 a day for it as well as have to call down to the front desk every day to get a new access code.The neighborhood is great, not nearly as crowded or frantic as midtown but with plenty of shopping, restaurants, and the amazing Fairway Market right across the street.There were some minor staff lapses, some just annoying, one a little bit more so.1.) One day I was expecting both a Fed Ex and UPS delivery so upon returning in the evening stopped at the front desk to see if they had arrived, in order to save myself the trip back down from the 21st floor to pick them up. The front desk said they had arrived and to pick them up from the concierge. The concierge went back to check, said they didn't have them and sent me back to the front desk. Frustrated, I went up to the room, only to find that both packages had been left in the room already. Great service, but why couldn't the concierge have known that the packages had already been brought to the room? On another day, I got another Fed Ex and this time, the concierge left a voice mail for me to come get it. A little consistency would be nice.2.) When I checked in, I was surprised that they didn't swipe a credit card for incidentals (the room was a direct bill to someone else.) A couple of days later I sent some dry cleaning with the valet, and when I got back, there was a voice mail to come down to the front desk and leave a credit card imprint before they would release my suit and shirts.3.) Finally, the first few days the room was fairly warm and I noticed the air conditioner in the living room wasn't cooling. I asked at the front desk for someone to come fix it and no one came. The next day someone came, took the lid off, pressed a button and pronounced it fixed, but it wasn't. Finally when I insisted the next day, someone else came and actually looked at the guts of the air conditioner to discover the compressor wasn't actually working. He changed the compressor later that evening and since then it worked fine.But, I still came to consider the Beacon home and look forwarding to returning for another ten days next summer.

<Author>bingojesus
<Content>Wouldn't stay anywhere else, now... We stayed at the Beacon for 10 days right at the end of June. It was our first ever visit to New York, and indeed the USA. We had the taxi trip from hell (we were taken right over to the East Side, at rush hour from Penn Station, the driver thinking we were going to the Beekman, despite me giving him the address of the Beacon...) so we were a bit frazzled to say the least when we pitched up at the lobby. But right from our arrival we were impressed with the friendly manner of the reception staff. Our room was on the 18th floor, one of the floors that has already been refurbished. While we were there, work was progressing on at least one other floor, but we were only aware of this when the lift stopped to allow a workman on or off. No disturbances to report. I assume that all the rooms will be refurbished eventually.We were delighted with our room. We were lucky to get a corner room at the back, which meant fantastic views over to the edge of Central Park. It was plenty big enough, finished to a really high standard, with a huge bed, TV to match and a useful well-equipped kitchenette. We really can't think of anything to even mention as a downside. The hotel is well-situated, the area is a lot less frantic than midtown. It's an easy walk to Central Park and with a good selection of bars, diners and restaurants nearby. The Fairway market across the street is open from 6:00am till after midnight and has everything you could possibly want in the way of food and drink. Zabars deli and HH Bagels are a short walk up Broadway and 72nd St subway station is about 3 minutes away in the opposite direction, so great for getting around. I know this reads like a brochure for the hotel, but we really did find it that good - and we are fairly critical travellers not afraid to register our displeasure if things aren't up to scratch. We plan to visit NYC again within the year, and having stayed at the Beacon we wouldn't entertain the idea of staying anywhere else.  
<Date>Jul 25, 2008

<Author>giberfam
<Content>Great Stay at the Beacon We stayed at the Beacon hotel for seven nights from June 17-24. We had initially booked a one bedroom suite but on check-in, the desk clerk looked at our family of four and upgraded us to a two bedroom suite for no extra charge. Our suite was huge and comfortable and quite clean. You just can't beat the space for the price. The staff was friendly and helpful. We really enjoyed the restaurant upstairs at the Fairway market. The food was great and really affordable - we ended up eating there several times. There is also a Starbucks right on the corner. I loved being in this area versus the much more crowded and commercial mid-town area.I actually had lived at the Beacon for a year back in the late 80's and they have definately done some remodelling since that time. We were on the 8th floor and it sounded like they were doing more remodelling on the floors above us but the noise was never intrusive. There is definately a lot of street noise (hey, it's New York) and we brought white noise machines which helped a lot with sleeping.The only negative experience was when we booked our return transportation to the airport through the concierge. he recommended we book a shuttle versus getting a cab since we were going to Newark. He told us, quite confidently that we would be the last stop on the shuttle and the trip would take about 45 minutes and so we had him book it for us. Well, when the shuttle arrived, the surly driver informed us that the Beacon is the first stop and the trip would take closer to an hour and a half. We ended up having to jump out in Midtown with all our luggage and hail a cab in order to get to the airport with enough time. It was no problem to get the cab driver to take us to Newark (despite what the concierge had told us). The fee for the shuttle was non-refundable so it ended up being quite expensive. It certainly seems like the concierge should have better information about this kind of thing.We would definately stay at the Beacon again (and just rely on a cab to go to the airport).  
<Date>Jul 7, 2008

<Author>leisa75
<Content>Fantastic - couldn't ask for better for the price.. We arrived into New York after a long stint holidaying in Europe.. and we fell absolutley in love with this city.The hotel Beacon is wonderful.. The price is great, the rooms are HUGE (in comparison to Europe), clean and tidy and it's in a great location on the lovely Upper West side, away from the tourism, hustle and bustle of Times Square.There was also a HUGE laundry with lots of washes and driers which makes that horrible holiday chore not so bad..Although there was no restaurant in the hotel, it definatley wasn't needed with Fairway Market Place across the road which stocked the most superb fresh fruit and vege and a wonderful selection of hot meals to go all at a rock bottom prices, even if you choose not to buy anything from here, it surely is worthwhile just to have a look. We figured it must be one of the best and cheapest places in town to grab something easy to eat as there was always a NY Police Department car or NY Fire Department truck out the front, a sure fire way to find a decent place - follow the locals! However there were many other different types of eateries just nearby. Central Park was just up the way and everything was relatively easy to access from the hotel including the sub.We are planning on going back to NYC in the not to distant future and we will be staying here again.... Thanks Beacon Hotel for making our stay in NYC a good one....

<Content>Happy with accomodation Stayed at this Hotel 9 years ago, and liked it then. It is on Broadway but a distance away from all the hustle and bustle of Midtown N.Y. I must admit I was a little wary of booking as I was informed the hotel was going through a refurbishment. But I neednt have worried, either it had been completed or we werelocated away from the work. <Author>stageold
<Content>Outstanding!! What a gem! I fell in love with the Hotel Beacon. It's meager star rating (due to lack of amenities I wouldn't use like an in-house restaurant or room service) does not do this property justice. I stayed in one of their renovated two-room suites on one of the top floors. I even had views of the Hudson River! I could easily have spent (and was prepared to spend) $500++ for a midtown hotel and not gotten as nice a room. My two-room suite was incredibly spacious, spotless and soothingly decorated. One side had a very comfortable living area with a dining table for four. The room also had a great fully equipped kitchenette with stove, refrigerator, and microwave. It was also fully stocked with plates, glasses and flatware, which I used for my take-out meal from gourmet grocer Citarella just across Broadway. There are other numerous dining options, including a great little diner adjacent to the hotel, Starbucks just a few steps away, plus plenty of restaurants of all types. Who needs a dreary hotel restaurant?!The bedroom side had a very comfy king bed, large flat screen TV with a bazillion channels of cable, and iPod docking station with speakers. The bathroom was small but beautiful  functional. The all-cotton towels felt great, and there was a full array of emergency items in case you forgot your toothbrush, razor, or needed to mend something.All in all, my stay greatly exceeded my expectations. The Hotel Beacon is a fabulous value for Manhattan, right smack in a great neighborhood and convenient even for my business appointment in midtown. This is now my go to hotel in NY.Note: The hotel is currently undergoing renovations, which always makes me shudder because of the potential noise  disruption. Don't let this scare you off. I can honestly say the renovations had no impact on my stay whatsoever. No renovation-related disruptions at all.

<Author>db1337
<Content>simple hotel, clean, good location, couple of problems I booked this hotel to have something convenient on the upper west side. It is a no-frills establishment, has the feeling of being slightly worn. A lot of reviews refer to it as a discovery, I think I read hidden gem and these lead me a bit astray.I arrived very late, and ill, and asked about room service (needed chicken soup). Got blank stares. Hotel doesn't have any such thing... oops. Good news is that there is a good restaurant next door that you can easily order up from so I got my soup, so perfectly fine by me.There was no real work desk, I couldn't set up my laptop easily. Hotel website says internet access is included in the room description. It costs $9.95, again no big deal, but I wish hotels would clarify if it is an added cost or not, I thought it was included.Room had very loud and not-very functional heating units. I had to wear earplugs. I had a suite with two rooms, the bedroom wouldn't heat at all. Room did contain a microwave and minifridge, which worked out well for me because I ordered a lot of soup when I got in (I was really not well, had flu) and was able to heat it up in the morning. Rooms were clean, just had that kind of worn feeling. Bed, and bedding were kind of in line with a 2.5 star establishment. After two days I left with a bill for $600 and didn't feel that this was really good value. Location is very good, right on the corner of Broadway and 75th.Doubt I will return, there was nothing really huge and negative, just seemed to be kind of expensive for what was provided. I usually would stay at the Omni and to my recollection paid about the same for a much better place, so I would go back to this the next time.

<Author>familyof4Adelaide
<Content>very run down but great location We stayed at the Beacon for seven nights in April last year. At first we were quite pleased as the foyer was nice and gave a good first impression. The room, however, left a lot to be desired. As we were travelling with our 5 and 7 year olds we booked a two room suite. It had two rooms and we chose to sleep on the fold out sofa bed as it was in the lounge area and it meant we could watch tv once kids had gone to bed. The sofa was incredibly uncomfortable and as a result we both had sore necks during our stay. The decor is very old fashioned and, although it was reasonably clean, it just didn't feel ''nice. The lifts were probably the worst thing about staying there as they were undergoing maintenance (apparently had been for some months!) and were very slow. More often than not we'd walk the ten floors to our room rather than wait. The staff were quite nice most of the time and the tour desk was great. NOW, so I don't sound like all I do is whinge, the location is great. There was nothing cooler than getting a cab and saying west 75th and broadway thanks'...so New York! lol It is a short walk to Central Park and Strawberry Fields, the subway and there is a big international market directly opposite. This was great, as our room had a kitchenette, we bought breakfast supplies/drinks, etc and kept them in our room. The cafe next door to the hotel is great for breakfast with friendly service. We just decided that in New York you are going to pay huge amounts of money for very little in terms of ''莽lass' . We did pay a lot less than we would have done had we stayed in Times Square or the like. However, it did little to detract from our New York experience on the whole. Would look elsewhere if we were to return.

<Author>kprawlings
<Content>The only place we stay in NYC I love this hotel. We stayed for our first time a couple of years ago and have done so several times. It is our little home away from home in New York City.THE BEACON IS FOR YOU IF:-You want to stay in a real neighborhood in Manhattan instead of in the middle of Times Square or right across the street from a tourist area. You're good with hopping on the subway around the corner and riding 10 minutes to the tourist traps.-You want a nice size, non-claustrophobic room that is clean and decent looking, but don't care about fancy decor or style.-You realize how expensive Manhattan is and that $300(ish) a night plus taxes is not going to get you a four or five star suite like it would in many other cities in the US.-You don't need pampering or care about the staff chasing after your bags, hailing cabs for you, and generally kissing your (--) during your stay! (They are, however, very nice.)The Beacon is GREAT! It is an amazing upper west side neighborhood that has a great feel to it. It has a huge market across the street for fresh produce and everything you need to stock your fridge in your room. (A huge and unusual benefit in Manhattan). There's a Starbucks next door, several great bars and restaurants only a five minute walk away. It's a five minute walk to Central Park. A ten or 15 minute subway ride to just about anywhere you want to go in the city. It is not fancy! Don't expect that! It's a 1.5 star hotel, which actually pleasantly surprised me the first time. If you are not loaded like us and can't spend thousands of dollars a trip on a hotel, it's a good choice over staying in a chain hotel for the same price or more and having a room a foot larger that the bed. Is it a bummer that Manhattan costs a fortune? Of course! If you can't wrap your brain around the expense, NYC is not for you. But it is amazing and worth every penny for me and my husband. We try to go at the holidays every couple years now.I didn't give an excellent rating, because in a perfect world you would get everything and more for this price. Considering the value, however, and the reasons mentioned above, I highly recommend the Beacon!

<Author>TroutGal
<Content>Hotel Beacon Great Neighborhood We stayed in 2 bedroom 2 bath suite for a long Christmas holiday weekend. We had a beautiful corner suite that was spacious and had 3 flat screen TVs. They are in the process of remodeling rooms and we had one of the finished ones. So make sure you ask for a remodelled room, if possible. The staff and concierge were extremely helpful and friendly. We felt safe and really loved the neighborhood. The wine store is next door and the grocery store across the street. This is a neighborhood with real families and people living here. The neighborhood services are good because they are not catering to tourists -- there are plenty of delis, pharmacies, bookstores, etc. And just 2 blocks from the 72nd street subway. We loved coming back from the crowded Times Square and Broadway area. It was a quick cab ride/subway ride back home to the hotel. It was so comforting coming back to escape all the insanity. We felt very safe and welcomed back to our neighborhood on 74th and Broadway. We would highly recommend this hotel for girls weekend in New York or for families. You will like eating next door at the Viand cafe for quick service, reasonable prices, and good food. You'll love shopping at the Fairway Market across the street and buy fresh fruit, cheeses, baked goods, etc. You'll be shopping with the locals. The worst thing that happened is that the large plate glass windows were sort of drafty and it was a little cool in the bedrooms, but we all slept well !! Don't overlook this hotel! It's priced fairly and it's in a great location!

<Author>lolow
<Content>Comfortable, accessible AND affordable in NYC! Hotel Beacon is in a great location for a short walk to events at Lincoln Center. The neighborhood also offers plenty of shopping, running the gamut from Barney's to Loehmann's. Our room was unusually spacious, comfortable and well-equipped ; the bathroom tiny but clean. In addition, you have a little kitchen with sink, fridge, stove, microware, coffeemaker, toaster, dishes  cookware,...everything needed for an extended stay. (There's also a coin-operated laundry in the hotel). Just next door is a cafe (sort of a Greek diner) which offers free delivery and reasonable prices for good food. The Hotel Beacon staff was very professional and friendly, and the hotel rates can't be beat for New York. We highly recommend it.

<Author>FAMILY44444
<Content>Yes if you want space No if you want tourist location or style The prior reviews are all pretty much on point. The review posted by 504 on 11/21 was right almost word for word, shabby window treatments, carpets, wallpaper, etc. Another poster described the stuff as faded.All true. It depends on what you want. For us (a family of 4) the one bedroom suite was by far the largest space we stayed in: thebedroom was around 12 x 14 and the living room was probably 12 x 20 -- huge by Manhattan standards. (see pictures) But the place was a little worn. We're used to Marriott's and this was a couple of grades below that.Location: this is not a tourist area; its more a neighborhood. I don't think theres much to do in Times Square (not into plays, ESPN, etc.) so I prefer not to stay there. This is an exiciting neighborhood with a real urban feel to it and just walking around is fun enough. The hotel is 2 blocks from the 72nd express stop on the Broadway line so its easy to get most anywhere, although at a fare of $2 - the $8 fare for a family of 4 adds up. Cab fare to the Chelsea galleries should be around $14; Canal Street should be about $18. If you want this neighborhood with some style try the On the Ave hotel 2 blocks north: more expensive and much smaller but very modern rooms.Food store: Best and cheapest is to shop in Fairway, the huge (by Manhattan standards) supermarket across the street or its better competitor 2 blocks north same side of the street. All the normal stuff in both stores plus tons of cheeses and prepared gourment foods. Worth a look even if you don't buy.Restaurants: Amsterdam and Columbus (the two street parallel to and east of Broadway) are loaded with restaurants -- walking and looking is fun by itself.Fast Food: The two pizza places north of the hotel on the east side of Broadway were (surprisingly for NY) mediocre to bad. If you want pizza, Little Nicks (2 blocks north, west side of Broadway) was outstanding. Gigi's, about 5 blocks south, west side of Broadway, had delicious quessadillas, and the Jewish deli (3 blocks north, east side of Broadway) was mediocre to good and a little expensive for fast food

We stayed three nights in mid-October, a very expensive time to stay in New York. I would definitely stay here again even if I could afford a better hotel. The service was fantastic. The room was clean and large by New York standards. The location was absolutely fabulous, so close to food, shopping, transportation, the park, etc. The rooms are in need of an update, but considering that everything functioned properly - windows open, air conditioner worked, plumbing, safe and elevator, I'll take shabby over chic. I've stayed in chic hotels in New York and stuff did not work, the rooms were so small you could touch the walls with both hands, and the service was yucky. So, the Beacon is it for me from now on!!

<Author>JLR
<Content>great location, good price It is always a challenge to find an affordable hotel in New York city. The Beacon was a good choice. I travel to New York often on business and each time I try to save the company a little money. The Beacon helped me to reach that goal. The hotel is located on Broadway near west 72 street and just a few steps away from the subway station so the location is great. There are many restaurants and shops nearby and a gormet supermarket right across the street. What I liked most about the Beacon in addition to the location is the friendliness of the staff. Check-in was very quick and pleasant. The rooms are a good size, not too small or cramped and they are equipped with a mini fridge, a range top, pots, dishes and a microwave. I could bring leftovers from the restaurant back to the hotel and heat it up for a late night snack. The decor is nothing to write home about, it's no Trump Tower. The wallpaper and carpet is little outdated and is starting to show signs of wear and tear along the edges but considering the bucks I'm saving I didn't mind at all. If you are looking for atmosphere and elegance this isn't the place but if you are looking for a comfortable budget hotel you will like the Beacon. I would stay here again because of the price and location. Staying in the Beacon is like staying in a nice well worn shoe, its comfortable.

<Author>heavybuddy
<Content>A great affordable choice in Manhattan Originally we were going to stay outside the city due to budget considerations, but after weighing the pros and cons decided that staying in Manhattan was worth the extra expense. It was the right decision. The Beacon is located in a great Upper West Side neighborhood, loaded with great stores and restaurants, and only a block from the 72nd St subway. You can be in Times Square in less than ten minutes, and from there it's easy to reach any part of NYC. This hotel is well suited to families, especially if you have a teenager that needs her privacy. Our suite was spacious by New York standards, with a well-appointed living room with a sofabed (which became my daughter's domain), a full kitchen, and a good-sized bedroom with two queen beds. We were on the 20th floor overlooking Broadway, which offered great views but was rather noisy throughout the night. The Fairway Market across the street is a great place to shop, but they take deliveries around the clock, and the trucks idle the whole time. If you're a light sleeper, demand a room at the back. I thought our suite was very nicely decorated, with no signs of wear and tear whatsoever. The beds were comfy, all the appliances worked, and we had plenty of towels and kitchen utensils. Although the traffic noise was constant, we never heard a peep from our neighbors, no running water, flushing, TV, nothing. The elevators were a bit slow but we never had to wait longer than 2 minutes. The housekeepers were friendly and gave us whatever we asked for no questions asked, but some of the people at the front desk could use a refresher course in customer service, or maybe a surgical procedure to remove their attitude. But there were also some very friendly clerks who went out of their way to help. Getting back to the Fairway, this is an incredible market, with an amazing selection of meats, cheeses, produce, and deli items, all very reasonably priced. The store is open until 1:00am, so my advice is go late at night, because in the afternoon and early evening the aisles are packed to the gills. If you're not into grocery shopping, there are dozens of great restaurants within a five minute walk. The Beacon is an ideal choice for people on a budget: for the price of an ordinary room in one of the big chain hotels in Times Square, you get a suite with a full kitchen, and room to relax. We were 100% satisfied with our stay and look forward to a return trip someday.  
<Date>Oct 24, 2007

<Content>The beacon really does shine!!!!!! :-) We have just returned from New york, and stayed at the beacon hotel, this was our 3rd visit to the city staying at various hotels/ Apartments each time, but the Beacon Hotel was by far the best!!, We booked a 1 bedroom suite, as we wanted space, and space is exactly what we got, our apartment in the hotel was huge compaired to others we have stayed in ( for the same price 2!! ), we had our own living room, with a sofa ( folded out in to a double bed) 2 chairs, a dining table with 2 chairs, coffee table, tv, with stand and storage space, the living room overlooked the hudson river, ( we were on the 24th floor) and it was a wicked view at night!, off the living room was a small but compact kitchen, and was spotless, and had everything we needed if we wanted to stay in and cook ( but who does in nyc), and the maid, which is daily service, left fresh coffee, teabags etc for us on the days we requested them to come in and change our sheets etc. The bathroom was a decent size, it had a bath and a shower, sink/ toilet, ( The maid also left us lil shampoos and conditioners etc, the mouthwash looked a bit toxic, but it was the thought that counted haha) The bedroom was huge, it had x2 double beds in (very comfy) and it had plenty of storage space, along with a tv and sky also in the room, it also had a personal safe ( free of charge) you could programme yourself, if you wanted to store your cash. The beacon hotel is about 5 mins from central park, and you could either walk, catch a cab or catch a sub if you wanted to go downtown where Macys, and to where all the other hustle and bustle is, The beacon hotel is brill for anyone, and it especially brill for the people who like to venture in to the hustle and bustle of new york when they fancy, but enjoy a more peacefull laid back pace where the hotel is situated, The Beacon hotel is just fab! :-) P.s Coney island is a must, although the cyclone  roallercoaster gives you some major bruises!! :-)

<Author>whits-endVA
<Content>Great for our family We stayed at the Beacon for two nights with our two children. When we walked into our king suite, we were obviously given a smoking room, but the front desk promptly and without question switched us to non-smoking (I should've asked when I made the reservation). The room was generously sized, so our family had plenty of room to stretch out. We enjoyed the neighborhood (nice wide sidewalk in front of the hotel) and the cleanliness and size of the 72d St. subway station. This was not the fanciest hotel in NYC, but it really hit the spot for our family. Our only regret was not being able to take better advantage of the adequately-stocked kitchenette- we ate at Sambucca nearby, and the food was awesome and plentiful. It was unfortunate that we left the next day and didn't have time to eat our leftovers for lunch!

<Author>stixvelo
<Content>Euro-style Simplicity in Upper Midtown We have stayed at the Beacon many, many times, and we consider it our home in New York. We have stayed at other, more upscale hotels farther downtown, and we always end up going back to the Beacon.  This hotel is very popular with french tourists, so it gives it a euro flavor. True, it is a one star hotel, without alot of amenities. But what they do, they do very well. The physical plant is well tended. Rooms are immaculate, service is efficient, warm and personable, and they consistenly remember the little touches, such as toiletries in the bathrooms. Concierges and front desk staff are excellent and knowledgeable. The real beauty of this hotel is its neighborhood. It is convenient to anywhere in New York -- not just Manhattan -- via the subway. Central Park, the Museum of Natural History, Columbus Circle, Lincoln Center, and the cheapest restaurants in Manhattan are within blocks of the Beacon. The local community is vibrant and alive. Local universities are convenient to get to as well. Fordham Law School, Julliard, Cooper Union, and Columbia U. are all close by or just a short subway ride away. The hotel is across from a Fairway supermarket, so you can get almost anything you need. And it's near Niko's, one of the best greek restaurants in New York. The hotel is an excellent value. The suites are huge, and they come wel-equipped with a studio-sized kitchen. We paid $255 per night. The only drawback to any hotel in Manhattan is parking. We paid $47 per night for parking, so factor that into your room budget. We enjoyed our stay here, and we will continue to make the Beacon our New York home.

<Author>Librarian1998
<Content>Roomy  The Hotel Beacon is not fancy. My daughter was disappointed when we pulled up and there was scaffolding covering the entrance of the hotel. However, it has everything a siteseeing family could need. The rooms are big by NYC standards - my kids had plenty of room to spread out their games.The neighborhood is great - a real residential neighborhood, as opposed to the Times Square area or the Wall Street area where we sometimes stay. There are plenty of markets, restaurants and stores at all price levels and tastes. We had breakfast a few times at the Tasty Cafe near the subway station (Broadway and 72nd, I think). This is a counter service place, but the food is great and quick, and there is a used book seller that sets up his stand right outside the door who encouraged the kids to look through his wares.Because the neighborhood is not as crowded and fast-paced as Midtown, we did not have to hold tightly onto our kids. The could enjoy looking around at a relaxed pace. Also, there is a fun playground with a Western theme at Amsterdam and 77th that my kids wanted to return to again and again.The concierge staff were very helpful. (They were the ones who directed us to the playground). Anything they couldn't answer, they looked up quickly for us. We didn't use them for anything high-end, like getting theater tickets, so don't know how they would do with that. A small thing, but a nice surprise was the toiletries in the room. Most hotels have a sign saying to ask the staff if there is anything you have forgotten, but Hotel Beacon anticipated everything for us, which is much better. The toiletries included things like cotton swabs and a toothbrush!We have stayed at the Hotel Excelsior in the same neighborhood. The Excelsior seems more up-to-date and upscale than the Beacon for a similar price. However, I preferred the Beacon because the staff was much more friendly and helpful, and the location is slightly closer to stores, restaurants and the subway. And even though the Beacon is in a busier location, we did not have any problem with noise in our room.

<Author>dsxl
<Content>Great deal for Manhattan We stayed only one night, but based on our experience we would definitely return to the Beacon. For a paltry (by NYC standards) $255 plus tax, four of us were more than comfortable in a one-bedroom (w/ two double beds) suite w/ kitchenette. The suite was large (and not just by NYC standards) and luckily for us had the added advantage of being a corner unit with great views (22nd floor). Our only minor complaints were beds that weren't quite firm enough and a bathroom that was a little on the small side. We didn't explore the area around the hotel, but as others have noted here, there are plenty of restaurants and a grocery store nearby, and it's a convenient enough location from which to get around the city. We were able to park on the street for free overnight, just around the block from the hotel. Overall this hotel is a very good value for Manhattan, at least compared to the half-dozen or so other places in the city, Brooklyn, and Secaucus where we've stayed over the last three years.

<Author>e-w-wimbledon
<Content>great value Don't normally take time to review hotels, but was so impressed with the Beacon that I made an exception. After reading so many horror stories of cupboard-sized rooms in New York hotels, we booked the Beacon after reading that the rooms were a good size. Even so, we were unprepared for the large bedroom + separate sitting room with kitchenette that greeted us when we arrived. We even had two flat-screen TVs! (We booked a kingsize suite through Expedia.)The decor is a little old and dated, but everything is clean. Our room had everything we could possibly need for our stay, and more. An excellent, price for what you get, especially when compared with prices elsewhere in New York. Central Park and subway within easy walking distance. Cafe next-door does superb, cheap breakfasts!

<Author>Stetsonz
<Content>Always a great experience We spent 4 nights at the Hotel Beacon beginning July 22. About ten years ago, we stayed at this property as part of a package deal, and really liked it. This year marks our fourth time to stay at the Beacon. We got the double double suite for 3 persons. This was a bedroom with 2 double beds and a seperate room that had a sitting room and a complete kitchen set-up. Having the extra room was handy for when one of us was up early we could go about things without awakening the others.  The lobby of the hotel has been totally renovated and is a lot brighter and roomier and has a much better floorplan. The room was neat and clean. The kitchen comes complete with microwave, stove, toaster, refrigerator/freezer, dishes and silverware. While we're not ones to cook in the room, one day it poured down rain so we crossed the street to Fairway Market and got some snacks and drinks. (Sidenote: The Fairway Market is a marvel unto itself. Huge variety and good pricing. You have to see it to appreciate it.)  It's true that the rooms are no showplace, but everything was clean and comfortable. That's all we really wanted. Generally we're not in the room a whole lot anyway. When you're tired from sightseeing all day, it doesn't matter if the comforter doesn't match the walls or if the sofa cushion design is a little worn. A USA Today newspaper is delivered to the door every morning, which is nice to have.  The only real downside to the visit was the elevators. In the past the elevators have been a little slow, but of no concern, but this time the wait time for elevators was sometimes quite long. There are notes saying they are working on them and directions on accessing the service elevators, but even that isn't always a help. Fortunately we were only on the seventh floor, so walking down was always an option, but only a necessity once. Hopefully they will get this improved, but even as it is, I'd stay there again.  Locationwise, this place is wonderfully situated. Not only is it across from the great market, it is a very short walk to a major subway stop. An express train can get you to 42nd street in a matter of minutes. One block over, Amsterdam Ave has a multitude of eating places, and just a couple more blocks you're in Central Park.  If I return to Manhattan one day, I will certainly check the Beacon for availability before I check elsewhere.

<Author>5onLily
<Content>Mixed results The hotel is in a great location and is less hurried than the east side and mid-town and is very close to the subway, Central Park, The Dakota's and museums. Great restaurants with larger portions at better prices than the east side and mid-town too. If only the rooms were as nice as the lobby. Some staff members were very pleasant while others were not that nice. Concierge's seemed to be bothered by our questions and on a couple of occasions gave us wrong information on restaurant locations. Customer service needs a lot of improvement here and it starts from the top. Some staff got it, especially in housekeeping who were very nice and attentive. Our problems were mainly in the lobby. We would give this place one more try but if customer service and cleanliness weren't improved, then it would definitely be the last stay here.

<Author>pearljam_49
<Content>The Place for parents with young kids!!! I recently jolned my wife, who was traveling on business, to NYC along with our two young children (4 yrs  2 yrs). We had a wonderful stay at Hotel Beacon.We received excellent service that was always friendly. Upon arrriving we asked for a crib and within 5 minutes we had it. Also, requested new sheets, coffee, and a roll a way and all were met within minutes. Housekeeping was professional and flexiable with nappings and all the like that come when traveling with young kids.We stayed in room 1911, which is a one bedroom. It was HUGE. The main room was 28 ft. x 16 ft., with a small kitchen (stove,oven,mircowave,full fridge, cups, glasses, toaster, etc.). There is a pull out bed along with a table and 3 chairs. The bedroom is also big 24 by 16 with a walk in closet. We were able to fit the crib in the closet, thus giving our children seperate rooms. THAT WAS GREAT.The only caution i have is beware of the locals on the elevators, very rude. But it is NY.Also, the hotel is a bit dated. Meaning the wall paper is old and so is some of the furniture. But in no way is it unclean or not comfortable. I felt this have the place some character. Nice break from the cookie cutter world we tend to live in these days.There is a laundry room on the 7th floor, containing 8 very clean washers and 8 well kept dryers. Each cycle cost $1.75.The location is awesome. 1,2,3 train is only a short 2 block walk. Fairway grocery is across the street, with excellent fresh produce and just about anything one would want. I read about the prices being high. NOT TRUE. With the kitchen in the room we saved big $$ eating breakfast, lunch, and a couple of dinners in the room.Eats- Big Nick's on broadway is a must. Their menu is extensive. We don't eat meat and were delighted to find well over 20 vegetarian offerings. Also try the Pizza shop on Amsterdam, something and Peppers, can't recall the full name.The park is about a 10 minute walk each way and worth it. For you will pass some truly beautiful brownstones. The Museum of Natural History is only about a 15 minute walk. For those of you with young kids in the park just after 81st street you will find the Dinana Ross Playground. Sand, fountain, swings (toddler and tire), and two huge playsets. Like every park in the city it's fenced in and well shaded.We did not use the wireless network, so can't comment either way. The next time we go to NYC it will once again be at the Hotel Beacon. LOVED IT!!!!!!!!

<Author>adventuretrip
<Content>Good Hotel in Great Area The Beacon Hotel is a great find, the rates are reasonable compared to many crazy priced Manhatten Hotels. Located on the Upper West side this district is packed with fabulous places to dine and shop and absorb yourself in NY culture. The hotel is only 2 minutes walk to the subway which has express trains to take you downtown within 10 minutes.Central Park and Riverside Park are also only a few minutes walk away and well worth exploring. Avis car hire just around the block and easy access onto the westside highway if driving out of the city.I have stayed here many many times and without a doubt would recommend it for business or pleasure........

<Author>AndyAtl
<Content>Heart of the Upper West Side, no complaints! Unless you are planning to spend serious money (these days, $650/night for a luxury hotel), you need to make some compromises in New York. Rooms are small; or the carpeting might be a little threadbare;or the elevators will be slow; or the staff might be rude. Or some combination of the above. It's simply what you have to expect in New York.By those standards, the Beacon was fantastic for me. I only stayed one night, so I didn't have time to use my fully equipped kitchenette(a great feature). OK, the elevators were very slow, but I only experienced one wait longer than a couple of minutes. My room was big -- much larger than other rooms I have had in the city. I lucked out with a 19th floor room on the southeastern corner,with eastward views of the famous Dakota apartment building and a sliver of Central Park, and southern views toward Columbus Circle.The room's furnishings weren't up-to-date and there were a few cigarette burns in the carpet. So what? If you want a design hotel you can look elsewhere. The a/c worked great, the bed was comfortable, the linens were clean, and so on. The room was huge and I had a sitting area with a table. This hotel even has a concierge, which is very rare for New York hotels in the moderate price range.The Fairway supermarket across the street is amazing, and I am running out of superlatives to describe the Citarella gourmet market next door (even the website will make a foodie drool). A few blocks away you can shop at the famous Zabar's. One New Yorker (a client I visited while in town) told me this is the best area in Manhattan for food shopping. So you literally can cook gourmet meals in your room -- or simply reheat some of the wonderful goodies from across the street. That will stretch your dining budget and allow you to splurge on other meals while you're out on the town.I met a friend for dinner and spent $160 (for two) at an Argentinean steak restaurant. It was a good meal, but I would have had just as much fun shopping for gourmet food and wine with my friend, and dining in my room with its city views. And we would have spent half as much.Eat breakfast at Big Nick's, a 24-hour Greek diner just up Broadway on the west side of the street. I enjoyed a great breakfast at an outdoor table. The service was friendly and the prices were reasonable.Being so close to the Broadway  72nd St. Subway station is a big plus. From that station you can take an express C train to 42nd Street in less than 10 minutes.

<Author>traveler123Boston
<Content>A bit disappointed I'm somewhat surprised at how positive these reviews are. We stayed at the Beacon for 3 nights and found it acceptable but not, I would say, worth the price. I would rate it somewhere below your average Marriott. The room looked old and run-down, though large, the bedding was thin and old, and there was no desk in the room (which was a suite), which is very odd for a hotel that has a business center. On the positive side, the housekeepers were very courteous, and the lobby area is pleasant. If you're on a budget, it's an okay choice, but I don't expect to return here. By the way, for out-of-towners, the location is very good.

<Author>Seattle_Ms_Fan
<Content>Perfect Location! I recently stayed for a week at the Beacon Hotel. I have lived in NYC and have traveled there countless times on business. I hate the big, convention style hotels and the miniture rooms at most of the boutique hotels. The Beacon had lots of room and none of the madness of the giant chains. We were prepared to wait for the elevators, having read the reviews. They were slow, but we came and went at off times and only had one annoyingly long wait. We took the freight elevators from the second floor and that worked out just fine. The proximity to the subway is great and it was an easy trip to any part of town. We went all over and never changed trains more than once. We certainly got our money's worth with the 7 day unlimited ride metro card! The Fairway market is amazing. And there are many great restaurants within a few blocks. We especially liked SaraBeth's at 80th and Amsterdam. It's known for breakfast, but the other meals are just as good. My only criticism was that the room was rather dated (although very clean). It sounds like they are re-doing the rooms and we should have requested an updated room (we didn't know better). The price was unbelievable, especially given the great location and size of the rooms! I will be back and have already recommended it to several friends and family members.

<Author>TravlingBard
<Content>Spacious, Courteous, Quaint I booked this hotel for two nights 4-11 through 4-13 to complement two nights on Times Square. The combination was brilliant. Hotel Beacon was convenient to places and events we wanted to visit, 3 blocks from the 72d St subway, and as a former NYC resident, I prefer the relaxed, funky mood of the West Side, the presence of dogs and baby carriages. The front desk was friendly and helpful as were the concierge/bell desk. Read reviews here so requested view room, stayed on the 23rd floor with a great view of the city and park in the distance. We were not too perturbed by slow elevators (also because of reviews). Got a pretty good deal on the website for a suite ($255 a night) which was huge by NYC standards. Two large rooms, the heat worked perfectly in both, nice kitchenette, small but clean polished stone bath. The older feel of the building truly made me feel at home and since all was clean, it was fine. Beds were okay, not too firm thank goodness, though a little bouncy perhaps. We arrived early and the staff were very very accomodating about holding our bags. The Fairway Market across the street is more than a neat little market - it's like a Whole Foods, Trader Joe's and international bazaar in one. I would have loved having it around when I lived in NYC and noticed many people taking cabs out of there with multiple bags. You could cook your own gourmet meals in the room with that kind of place so close, but why when there are so many wonderful and reasonable places to eat nearby (choices choices). We ate at San Luigi, an Italian place at 311 Amsterdam just one block over offering homemade pasta, very good bread, and other highly authentic Italian home cooking - pasta dishes for under $20, meat and fish for under $30. Excellent wine. Did I mention there's a Starbucks on the corner? Sit in the window for some really good people-watching. As for Hotel Beacon, I'd stay there again in a heartbeat and there's no other place you need on the West Side unless you MUST have 5 star.

<Author>NolaCooke2162
<Content>Good value at the Beacon My husband and I just spent 10 nights at the Beacon, in the Upper West side of NYC. We loved the location and enjoyed our stay, despite a few hiccups here and there. Like other people, we had occasional trouble with the elevators; and the toilet blocked twice in the first 3 days, the first time at midnight on the night of our late arrival, after a 30 hour trip, so that wasn't fun. Each time we reported it, however, the staff responded with exemplary speed and efficiency. Finally I just closed the tap slightly so the bowl did not fill up quickly and the problem disappeared.We chose the Beacon because of its general location and because we could self-cater when we wanted. (Be warned, however, that the extractor fan is connected to the stove top, so if you are making toast it does not come on, and the smoke alarm is pretty sensitive! We were caught twice, and that was once too often!) It was great to be able to shop at the wonderful Fairway market directly across the road, especially at 10.00pm on the Sunday night of our arrival. It was even better to eat in the upstairs Steakhouse Cafe, whose $29 three course meal was wonderful, good food and great value. We found the beds pretty comfortable and the decor subdued but restful. The size of the room was a great plus, as was the comfortable furniture in it. All in all, the Beacon delivered everything I expected from tripadvisor comments, and we would certainly recommend it, as well as stay there again ourselves.

<Author>Jilll
<Content>Great Hotel for its price We have just had four nights at the Beacon from March 21st to 25th. I thought for the price we paid we got a good deal (439.00) for four nights for the two of us. We had no probs checking in, got a non smoking room as requested on the 23rd floor. No noise at all any night and the kitchenette with microwave, two cooking rings, full size fridge, kettle, toaster and coffee maker all provided, as was the actual tea and coffee. They even provide a bottle of washing up liquid. Its not the Ritz, but you get what you pay for. The room was large. 2 double beds, sheets changed every day, TV, table dining chairs, and lounge chair. Bathroom was spotless, as were the rooms. It does look a little dated, but the hotel is quite old, and is always full all year round. They are having an upgrade on the elevators and there are signs posted so that you can go round the back of elevators and use the service lifts. We seemed to be the only people who did this and never had to wait more than two minutes for elevator, yet people were complaining at the front desk about it. Its a stones throw from the subway, which was very handy, and its good to get away from the noise of the sirens and hustle and bustle of Times Square. This part of town is very handy to get to Central Park (2 blocks away) and especially for my hubby who is a life long Beatles fan and wished to visit John Lennons Memorial (which we had to do every day). If you want to pay top dollar you can do, but I would deffo stay at the Beacon again. At just over 拢50 each per night I think it was well worth it.

<Author>sheshistory
<Content>Problematic Visit to Hotel Beacon I stayed at Hotel Beacon in March during a visit to New York City.The first problem was the parking. While this might not have necessarily been the hotel's fault, since I was driving in from the airport, I wanted to make arrangements. I was told by two different associates at the hotel that nearby parking was available. When I found the parking garage and others by it, they were filled so I ended up driving around for an hour for a spot on the street.Check in was prompt and friendly. I went up to my room having ordered the wireless internet access for $9.95 per 24 hours. First the television did not work so they sent someone up to fix it. The television was very temperamental so once the man got it working, it went out again. Then again. Well, I didn't come to watch television, so I dealt with it. Then I tried to sign on to the internet, which did not work either. Luckily, I called the internet help desk and the problem was corrected in short order.Sleeping was an issue here. The first night, since the televisions are set against the headboards of the next room, I heard my neighbor watching television until 4 AM. It wasn't a sound sleep. The next night there was an outrageous set of people in the rooms surrounding mine that were screaming and slamming doors until 6 AM. The hotel management did nothing. The hotel lobby is very nice however the rooms are a bit worn, with peeling wallpaper and worn carpet but overall, were clean and the bathroom was quite nice and well stocked. The room had a kitchenette with a coffee maker, refridgerator, and sink, which was nice. The best part of this hotel is the location - this isn't in the middle of Times Square but in a great neighborhood with cute restaurants, stores, and entertainment within a few steps. There was even a grocery store right across the street, which was wonderful. The hotel is right near Central Park and other points of interest.Overall, Hotel Beacon is a fairly good value for New York City and is in a great location. However, if you want a quiet and sound night's sleep, this might not be the place for you.

<Author>PigsFly
<Content>A good value for the value-oriented traveler I've stayed here maybe a half dozen times over the years and find it to be a good value for the value oriented traveler. If you are a high-end traveler who likes to be spoiled, this might not be for you. If you are a backpacker who wants to travel on the cheap, this probably isn't for you. But if you like a comfortable, safe, well located hotel, quiet and conveniently located with few amenities, this is it. We had a double double this time -- essentially a suite -- with a small kitchen, living area and two double beds. It was clean, well kept, and affordable. Most of all it is quiet. The elevators are a bit dicey (we were offered use of a service elevator) and there's no restaurant (a lunch place is next door), but it came in about $100-200 less than its counterparts. We found the staff to be more than accommodating and best of all, it's a stone's throw from the 72nd St Subway and CPW. We zipped all around, slept well, and general felt cared for. I recommend it for the mid-price traveler who likes convenience, safety, and a modicum of comfort.

<Author>luna99
<Content>Thought it was pretty nice and would stay again. I should have written this a long time ago... let's see if my memory serves me well.. here we go!My sister came to visit me in central new york during may of 2006 so my fiance and I naturally wanted to take her to NYC, she had never been. We decided on the Beacon because we got a broadway show and hotel package and it was a pretty good deal. Check in I remember was pretty easy and I thought the rooms were decent sizes.. we had two beds and my fiance and I had to share one which was a little crowded but we didn't mind. I do remember the beds not being all that comfortable and the room does look a little dated as far as the decor goes..but it was clean and had enough room for the three of us. I do remember really liking the bathroom (I'm super picky about bathrooms). It was small but clean and looked like it had been updated and had new applicances in there. There was also a small kitchen type area that we didn't use but would have been great if we decided to.What I love most about this place is the location! There is so much great stuff really close by.. the market across the street (where my fiance went one night to get snacks for us)... the cafe on the corner.. we ate breakfast there the morning we had to leave and really enjoyed it. Central park isn't far.. there is a lush store ([--] - bath products) nearby which really made me happy ..and the walk to the subway isn't bad either.I really like this part of town because it felt like families lived there... and riverside park is close by.. we walked there one early morning and saw a lot of people walking their dogs or jogging. Early mornings in NYC are soooo nice.This is only my third time to go to NYC, but the first time I stayed in a swanky place in time square which of course was great and the second time we stayed in a youth hostel which was ok too... I feel like the beacon is somewhere in between. If you can get past the old decor of the room... you're set.I even asked the concierge once about where a good place for pizza would be and he directed me somewhere and was super friendly and nice.I'd stay here again for sure. Hope this review helps!

<Author>summitsw
<Content>Nice Hotel We'd stayed at the Beacon before back in 98 and so chose it again for that reason. It's a nice hotel in a great location, we walked from Times Square every day. There's a market across the street, and the restaurant next door delivers free of charge and has good food at good prices.We had a one bedroom suite and the kitchenette was great. Also good having a tv in the bedroom and lounge room as it made it easier for everyone to watch what they wanted. Bathroom was tiny, but clean and extra towels etc provided quickly when we asked. The bedroom and lounge rooms were big and lots of closet space. The rooms are a bit dated though.The staff were friendly, although I agree with other reviews about the hotel staff refusing to get you a cab, although we didn't have any trouble hailing one when we needed it. There's internet available downstairs. The elevators were out of commission a few times during our stay due to new ones being installed. The only downside was the noise. I saw someone say they were on the 15th floor above Fairways (the market) and couldn't hear anything, well we were on the 20th floor above Fairways and the traffic noise was ridiculous. I had to resort to earplugs to get any sleep and seriously considered asking to be moved to a different room but couldn't be bothered. All in all though I'd stay there again if I was in NY.

<Author>ann99bray
<Content>Disappointing, needs overhaul We stayed at the Hotel Beacon for 3 nights the middle of December. I had a hard time getting a hotel for a reasonable price and settled on the Beacon after reading the reviews on this site. We were definitely disappointed. The first room we were put in was a small, shabby room that was a smoking room. I asked to be moved because of the smoky smell in the room. The management agreed to move us, but pointed out that they could not gaurantee a non-smoking room. The second room was somewhat better and had more room. On the plus side, housekeeping was very good and the towels were very clean and soft. The hotel is close to a subway, some decent diners and a wonderful market and deli across the street. We did take cabs a lot and hailed our own cab. The conceirge booked a shuttle to the airport for us when we were leaving. We used the fridge in the room and also the tea kettle. I would stay here again mainly because it was the most reasonably priced hotel that I could find in a decent area. It is definitely better than staying in mid-town which is so crowded and expensive. I would also think it might be a good choice for families.

<Author>kprawl
<Content>A great choice for NYC! We stayed at the Beacon after doing thorough research on tripadvisor and other sites. Being that it's a one star hotel, I expected it to be decent for the value but not much more.We were wrong! We ended up loving the Beacon and have found our place to stay when we're in New York. The one bedroom suite was huge, had a kitchenette, was very clean. As you've heard from others, the neighborhood could not be better. The Upper West side has a great NY feel--visiting Times Square was a lot of fun, but I wouldn't want to be plopped right in the middle of it in a cramped and overpriced hotel room.Some other plusses--the Starbucks right next door, the great market across the street (that incidentally all you lymies like my husband had tons of English stuff including every English candy bar you could want!), was a five minute walk to the subway, and a ten minute walk to Central Park. My husband's a runner and ran every day there. The hotel was much nicer than I expected. I'd say that unless you're a high maintenance traveler with expectations of people waiting on you hand and foot like in a chain hotel or the more expensive variety, you'll like it. No they didn't call a cab for us (we didn't ask). It's on Broadway for God's sake, it takes like 30 seconds to hail a cab to take you to the airport! Yes, we carried our luggage up, no there isn't room service (although a restaurant delivers there that we didn't use) You get the gist--it's a one star hotel so it isn't going to be perfect. The staff however was fine, no complaints whatsoever. Anyway, bottom line is that for the value, it was a great experience. By the time we left it felt like our little home away from home. We're going back in May with family and after this test run, we will always recommend the Beacon.By the way, price out a one bedroom vs. a standard room--it wasn't much more and was so nice to have a separate living area. Also, they'll give you a few bucks off for a AAA discount.

<Author>Sword1
<Content>Perfect Hotel My wife and I stayed at the Hotel Beacon from Nov 29th to Dec 3rd 2006 for our 4 night trip from Dublin, Ireland. We chose this having read many reviews from other Trip Advisor reviewers of various hotels. I have to say from the outset that we loved the location and the hotel itself and we were very impressed with the rooms (1 Bed Suite with Sitting Room  Kitchenette). They were huge and very clean. The bed-room included a walk in closet as did the hallway - very handy for stashing cases as well as clothes. The kitchenette is a nice feature although we didn't really use it much but the fridge is handy for storing water etc. Decor is a little dated being a bit flowery  patterned but unless you're a complete fusspot this is not a major concern. Rooms were cleaned daily and USA Today delivered to door every morning. Location is excellent with the fairways market across the road for any necessities and the Manhattan diner 2 blocks north for breakfast and a Sarbucks virtually next door if you need it . The Beacon is also very close to the many restaurants etc on Columbus AvePrevious reporters here mentioned noise at night but we were on the 15th floor overlooking fairways and can tell you that we heard nothing! The hotel itself doesn't have a bar or restaurant but that's not a concern for us as we never eat where we'er staying anyway. We prefer to get out and eat with the locals. The Beacon is just 3 blocks (3 mins) from 72nd St Subway which is served by the 1,2  3 lines. It's 2 stops to Columbus Circle and 4 stops from Times Square with Macy's on 34th St one stop further down the line at Penn Station. Too Handy! The same subway will also take you right down to lower manhattan and Ground Zero. All in all a great place to stay and would recommend it to anybody. Not necessarily a honeymoon spot but great for every other reason to visit NY. Big thumbs up and will definitely stay here again.

<Content>Beacon Hotel - Ideal The Beacon Hotel is fine, rooms are large and clean. <Author>Culture_Lover
<Content>Good location, spacious, comfortable This hotel was ideal for our needs on this trip. It is a reasonable walk from Lincoln Center, convenient to a good subway line (with direct connection to Penn Station), and surrounded by a residential neighborhood, so area restaurants have to stand or fall based on return business rather than a convenient location for tourists. The kitchenette, while very small, had a stove, oven, toaster, coffeemaker, and refrigerator, and a basic set of dishes and cookware (probably a microwave too, but we didn't use one so I don't remember), and there is a very extensive grocery store right across the street, so it is quite feasible to make your own simple breakfasts and pack lunches if you want to ease the financial stress of doing things in Manhattan. (The hotel is an excellent deal compared with others in Manhattan, but it's still well over $200/night). The restaurant connected with the hotel is not fancy but quite good. A few tips: the fitness center was closed for renovation when we were there in late November of 2006. Wireless internet is available for $10/day; there's also an internet center on the second floor that we didn't use but I believe is free to guests who sign up to use it at the front desk. The bathroom is not large and has a tile floor that can be cold, so I wished I had packed a pair of slippers. The concierge can arrange for Super-shuttle service to the airports for about $20/person. I did this and it worked out well, although it is a good idea to leave extra time for the shuttle to get through Manhattan traffic to pick up people at other hotels.

<Author>Monroe1953
<Content>Hotel Beacon was great! I had researched the Hotel Beacon on Tripadvisor and it certainly lived up to me expectations. My daughter and I stayed for 4 days at the beginning of November. Our room was a good size, clean, with fresh towels every day and basically everything we needed for our stay. We found a lovely place called Gigi's for breakfast near the subway stop on 72nd street and felt extremely safe in the area around the hotel. We are hoping to return to NYC as soon as possible and will definitely be staying at the Hotel Beacon again and again and would also recommend it to anyone.
