<Author>chissis
<Content>Perfect home away from home Several friends from around the country met in New York from September 16th through 21st. Three of us stayed at the Hotel Beacon, and we couldn't have been happier. We had a suite with two double beds and a hide a bed in the livingroom. There were two very nice size closets, one in the bedroom and one in the hall. Both the bedroom and the living room were large with wonderful views overlooking the Hudson River. The kitchenette had a stove, oven, toaster, coffee pot, microwave and apartment size refrigerator, as well as cups, plates, utinsels, and dish towels. The bathroom was nicely appointed, and the rooms were clean and fresh. We called for extra towels (women, you know need a lot of towels) and they were quickly brought up. There was no noise between rooms at all, you couldn't tell there was anyone else on the floor. We requested non-smoking, and the room was truly that - no old smoke odors at all, in fact none in the hall either.The elevators were clean and fast, and the staff was very nice and courteous. We couldn't have asked for a nicer place from which to venture out - The Beacon is close to everything - subway, shops, restaurant, park, and historic buildings, and it truly was a home away from home. We can't wait to return!  
<Date>Sep 28, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A bit run down, but great location We spent 3 nights at the Beacon in June 2004 and found it a bit more run down than at our last visit in 2001. The furniture and carpeting are shabby and the A/C in one of the rooms did not work. The bathroom, however, was nice and bright and seemed to have been renovated recently. Like the last time, we had a suite and found that the quality of the equipment in the kitchenette had also gone down. But perhaps help is on the way: Major renovation work was going on in the reception area during our stay -- hopefully those efforts will expand to the rest of the hotel.These shortcomings are compensated for by the hotel's excellent location on the Upper West Side, 3 blocks from the 72 Street subway station. There is a wonderful market across the street (Fairway) where we bought terrific breakfast and take-out dinner items to save on restaurant expenses. Rooms facing the street have a noise level that can be expected in a big city, but be aware that also rooms facing the courtyard are noisy when there are concerts at the adjacent Beacon Theater.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Safe, clean, spectacular view I was in a suite on the 20th floor, at the southernmost tip of the hotel. Illness kept me indoors at night. But the view of the Ansonia looking west across Broadway--turrets, gargoyles, chimneys, etc.--was spectacular. Housekeeping excellent, staff friendly and professional. If you love the upper west side or are lucky enough to afford a suite with a view like this, you can't do better for the price.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great for the budget traveler I typically frequent hostels, since I travel alone and have a limited budget. This time, I decided to upgrade, and I wasn't disappointed. Definitely not a first-class hotel, but if you're looking for a comfortable room in a great location, then the Beacon is perfect. Affordably priced with all the right accomodations. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not bad WHEN: Stayed May 7-12. Two adults.ROOM: Guestroom with double beds and kitchenetteFIRST IMPRESSION: Room isn't your upscale type of hotel room but it isn't your Motel 6 either. It definitely is bigger than your budget NYC hotel room. Good size for the price. Didn't have a view but faced the sidestreet; didn't have any noise from the street like I've read. We slept well through the nights. Perhaps the rooms facing Broadway Avenue may have had more noise? The carpet looked a bit dingy. The beds were comfortable; firm. Small table with two chairs provided. Dresser with two larger drawers. TV with cable. Shades that you could roll up or down by simply pulling on a cord. AC worked well. Alarm clock available. Iron and board in small closet.KITCHENETTE: Microwave, electric stove, and small refrigerator. You also are provided with plates and utensils for four people. We made ourselves breakfast burritos each morning! In addition there is a nonstick pan, a couple of serving utensils, and a toaster! BATHROOM: Very small. Bathtub/shower combo. Not too much counterspace. Toilet with strong flush.STAFF: Not overly friendly but then we're not ones to ask for a lot and complain.LOCATION: Upper West SideHOTEL BEACON NEIGHBORS: Fairway Market is right across the street and closes at 130am. You can get fruit, eggs, various meat, etc. If you're more interested in gourmet type groceries then you can head uptown to Zabar's which is about 7 blocks away (80th Street). Starbucks is practically next door on the right. Vivaldi cafe is literally next to the entrance. TRANSPORTATION: **SUBWAY**About a block and half from the subway, 2 minute walk; 72nd Street stop to be exact. Jump on the Red 1, 2, 3, or 9 line and that'll take you straight to Battery Park (South Ferry stop) if you go downtown with various stops such as Times Square and Columbus Circle (Central Park). **TAXI**Easy to hail a cab as soon as you step out on the sidewalk. RENOVATION: They are currently having some work done to update their really small lobby. Should be complete by midsummer. Noise is not bothersome. We were out all day and only really just pass through the lobby so the work being done was not a nuisance. They do have fairly quick elevators (3). **All in all, we would consider staying here again on our next visit although we would also consider trying out another more upscale hotel such as the Marriott or Sheraton just to see what a regular hotel room in this type of hotel would be like. But only if the price is right. Hope this helped. Post any questions as I regularly review this site.  
<Date>May 15, 2004

<Author>gardgal
<Content>We will be back! Just returned from 6 nights at the Beacon (May 1-7, 2004). Our room was a GIGANTIC deluxe king room with kitchenette. It was very handy to have fridge and microwave for restaurant leftovers. The stove burners shorted out at times, but worked well enough for our purposes. No view, but they offered to move us to a view room when it came available next day. The room was very clean and quiet except during concerts at the Beacon Theater directly underneath us.The price was 1/3 less than a kitchenette suite in the Doubletree Times Square, with a much nicer neighborhood and ambience. Friendly concierge, outstanding location with museums, shops, Central Park, and cafes in walking distance. The rest of New York easily reached by subway. We got 7 Day Unlimited Metro Cards for $21 and rode all over. We have visited the city many times before, but never overnight. We did a lot, but missed a lot and will be back to the Beacon for more.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent hotel  This hotel is a true find, especially for wheelchair users and disabled travelers. Upon arrival, a separate entrance then a ramp lead you to the front desk. The staff is courteous and thoughtful.The room we had was a one bedroom suite, and it was hands-down the most wheelchair accessible hotel room we've ever stayed in.The bathroom featured marble floors and roll-in shower, a bath chair is available in the hall closet. The kitchenette was obviously recently renovated with marble floors, brand-new cabinets, full-sized fridge, as well as a microwave, coffee maker and mini-stove. Pots, pans, plates and silverware are all there. Just pick up some groceries and you're good to go for days. The kitchen and bathroom sinks are open underneath, no problem if you use a wheelchair.The nicely appointed living room featured a pull-out couch, kitchenette table, comfy chairs and coffee and end tables. The bedroom was more than adequately-sized, featuring a closet with lowered hanging area. Comfy pillows and soft blankets made for a restful night after touring Manhattan.All doors in the apartment (I call it that because it was bigger than some of our NY relatives' pads!) are extra-wide. The window shades are easily lowered and raised with a reachable pulley chain.Need anything? The concierge is helpful and at the ready. A gem on Broadway, the Hotel Beacon will be our home away from home when visiting Manhattan. Thanks to the staff and management for a wonderful stay.

<Author>Charger_Fanatic
<Content>A real gem in a lively neighborhood! A wonderful stay. My wife and I just returned from a six night stay at The Beacon along with our two young boys as a special treat over their spring break from grade school. I'm pleased to report that it suited our needs very well. We selected this hotel on the strength of the many positive reviews we read on this website, and the favorable press is well-justified. The location is 75th and Broadway, and there are many amenities within the immediate area of the hotel: Grocery stores, pubs/bars, upscale eateries, family diners, budget fast food, drug and department stores--you name it. There are two subway stations within a short walk in opposite directions of the hotel, and you can get anywhere in Manhattan from there. The closet space is excellent, and the hotel, while not particuarly lavish, is certainly clean and well-managed. A minor negative is that we did hear some street noise even though we were on the 22nd floor, but then again that's pretty much par for the course in a city like NYC unless you're staying in some posh hotel. It wasn't so bad as to keep us awake, or anything of the sort. The simple fact is that this hotel a terrific choice for a family of four or less, particularly if young kids are in the picture. The kitchenette (complete with a stove and a good sized refrigerator/freezer) is a huge plus, and very hard to find in NYC hotels. We had breakfast in our room each morning, munching on all kinds of great stuff from the Fairway Market directly across the street. We wouldn't hesitate to stay at The Beacon again in the future. You could do MUCH worse.  
<Date>Apr 15, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Beacon shines brightly on the Upper West Side A good friend told me about Hotel Beacon, and after reading all the other reviews, we booked for Dec. 21 to Dec. 27. From the moment we arrived until the bill was taken care of, we could not have had a more pleasant experience. The lobby was elegantly decorated for Christmas. The room was very comfortable (but admittedly, the beds were somewhat hard; nevertheless, we slept just fine), and having the kitchenette made life so much easier. Everything was kept sparkling clean throughout our stay-plenty of strong, hot water for baths...A booklet in the room gives suggestions on where to eat, and the places that we tried matched what was said. Good markets and stores all around, and having the subway all of a minute away was great. People who stayed at the hotel were friendly-maybe we all felt lucky to have a find or it could have been the holiday spirit? There were two concierges, both of whom were extremely conscientious and helpful. It's true there's street noise, but on the upper floors, it doesn't seem to be in evidence. A definite find.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great base for NYC Nothing much to say that people havent put already! The hotel is has a great location, is well worth the money. The restaurants arent as expensive as Midtown areas can be, the subway is an express subway too with disabled lifts and operates all night, the 104 bus stops outside the hotel and there are 2 decent supermarkets (one is 24 hour) over the road.TIP: order takeout for Ollies noodles (or walk 8 block down broadway) great chinese food.The only negative point would be the size of room and the storage available, if you had 4 adults then you would find it cramped but then again I am only nitpicking.Would definately (and will definately) stop here again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>couldn't be happier We were attending a wedding in NYC the day before Thanksgiving and were extremely pleased with the hotel. First of all, the location was perfect for our purposes, e.g. the reception at Tavern on the Green and the rehearsal dinner. Also, we could walk 3-4 blocks to the site of the inflation of the balloons which our 6 year old enjoyed. The neighborhood felt safe and had many restaurants and shops. The staff at the front desk was friendly and efficient. The one bedroom suite was clean and VERY spacious. The linens were clean. The bed comfortable. The handicapped accessible bathroom was newly renovated and easy to use for all (handicapped and otherwise). The in-room safe was most useful. The kitchen had full amenities and was very clean. Considering that most restaurants will deliver, the kitchen became an important feature. All of the other wedding guests enjoyed the hotel as well. No complaints as far as we know. I was surprised at the low room rate, $185.00/night for the 1 bedroom suite! We had stayed in the Sheraton Towers in the past and felt that Hotel Beacon was superior especially if you consider the price. We will definitely stay at this hotel again in future visits of which there will be many I'm sure.

<Author>mainegad
<Content>Loved this hotel in NYC's most livable neighborhood My family stayed at the Beacon in September. The hotel had a lot to live up to. In past trips, we had stayed in the very nice Roger Smith Hotel in midtown. This time, we wanted to enjoy the more neighborhoody feel of the Upper West Side. The Beacon turned out to be a prize. The rooms in this former apt. house were comfortable and clean and fairly large. There was a small kitchenette with two-burner stove, half-size fridge and microwave. Dishes and cookware were available. The wonderful Fairway Market (groceries) was directly across the street from the hotel, making it very simple to find great food and cook in our room. Both HH Bagel and Zabars were right down the street. And the 72nd Street subway stop was about a two-minute walk from the hotel. The Upper West Side is a wonderful neighborhood, with a vibrant street-life. But it isn't quite as crazy as the Village or as sterile as midtown. We're definitely staying here again.  
<Date>Oct 6, 2003

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfection on the Upper West Side The Beacon was a perfect hotel. It was one block off the subway, across the street (literally!) from the Fairway Market, just a few blocks from Zabars, a few blocks from Central Park and incredibly comfortable. The room was pretty large by NYC standards with an effective air conditioning system and easy to use lights and TV. The bed was comfortable, the kitchenette was great and the bathroom was very clean and comfortable.I recommend asking for a room on one of the higher floors to enhance your view and decrease traffic noise. We were on the 14th floor and the traffic was not a problem at all. I cannot overemphasize the terrific location and ease of staying at the Beacon. I highly recommend it and will stay again the next time we're in NYC.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Hotel Beacon: Worth far more than what I payed. Recently I had to fly into NYC for a small convention. I knew that my weekend would be free and I wanted to be closer to the culture of city. I really wanted to avoid the constant buzz and flash of Times Square, and the shuffling of money in the business and financial district. I finally chose the Hotel Beacon based on price and location. It's in a great location on the Upper West Side. They were offering a special on their one bedroom suites that I just couldn't pass up. It was well worth it because I had an excellent view of Central Park, a kitchen, and the rooms were quite large compared to most NYC hotels I have stayed in throughout the past. I had a one bedroom suite for only $180/nt and it had a kitchenette with all the dishes and everything I needed. I think the Beacon's regular rooms have kitchenettes too. I couldn't imagine being in a better location for what I needed. Just about everything I did while in the city I did it within a 10 block radius. I was right next to Lincoln Center, Museum of Natural History, Central Park, the Rose Center, and an abundance of food and entertainment for when the sun went down. The neighborhood felt very safe and the tree-lined streets were a very nice touch to top it off with. Overall, I couldnt imagine staying anywhere else in the city. However, my only complaint would be the lack of intrusive lights and sounds that used to interrupt my sleep before I found this place. I definitely expected to pay much more for such high ceilings, the marble bathroom, and all great staff. I'll definitely stay at the Beacon next time I am in New York  
<Date>Jul 1, 2003
